**Chapter XVIII**

Chapter XXX.
Eradication of teeth.
Understand that you cure the tooth from its pain using all means and take your time in the complete eradication of it, for there is no reason to delay the moment of its extraction, as it is a sublime substance whose excuse lies in the eradication of itself.
You may also understand that when the patient is compelled to have a tooth eradicated, you must be firmly certain which tooth is causing the pain, as the deceiving pain may come from the illness and not from the healthy teeth, and you eradicate that one, but the pain does not cease until the sick and painful tooth is eradicated, for we have seen this in the operation of the barbies.
Therefore, once you have determined which tooth is painful and know its location well, you will need to scrape the area around the tooth with a spatula, ensuring it has some virtue, until it is completely separated from the gums, and then apply pressure with your fingers or use small pliers gradually until it loosens.
Then apply a strong, firm grip using large pliers or similar tools for good manipulation or extraction, and hold the patient's jaw between your fingers so that it does not move, and treat the tooth according to its position in such a way as not to break it or cause the patient greater pain.
And if this is not forgotten, take one of those instruments, place it around the tooth from all sides with ease and effort, and attempt its removal as if it had just begun.

Chapter XL.
In which the entire discourse is focused on the diagnosis and treatment of apoplexy.

And if you wish, open it again with your hand; and since you must be on the ground, place the patient's head at the back of your fist, the length of which should be an arm, and their head at the back of the other fist precisely two fists long; and the distance between each fist should be a palm, and already there will be a trace in each fist where the flow returns, and every part is firmly pressed to the ground so that no more pain occurs.
And take another fist-sized round object on which the flow turns, and turn it in both directions between the two fists.
And at the end of it, there is a trace where the object turns, the length of which is a palm where it turns; and in both other fists, they are similar to that one.
Then tighten the ligaments you have straightened on the patient's foot at the point where their head is placed, and the ligaments you have tightened on their thighs at the turn which is opposite their legs.
And then you should take each turn and have a minister twist the turn with their hand, and the doctor bend the spine as we have said.
Then, when the spine is returned to its place and the position is adjusted, cover it with a dry, clean bandage, and stop. Then place your hand over the bandage, starting from the table, where its width should be about three times or so the length of the affected area, and along the part of the spine.
And then, using the treatment we have mentioned, observe the patient's condition and provide them with subtle, nutritious food until they are healed.
And if any danger is perceived in the area at the end of healing, then medications that soften and soothe should be administered orally for a long time, as we have recommended; this can also be done by applying a thin layer of lead on that place.
And in some cases, there occurs an urgency in the rear of the spinal bones, and it is separated due to that dislocation; and it is that bone which you should already consider as imminently dangerous because it will cause great pain if this medicine is not promptly applied to it, for it can lead to death.
**Capitol XXXI.**
**On the Cure for a Dislocated Hip.**
You know that the joint of the hip and the joint of the muscle should not be displaced so much, and this only happens to those whose other joints experience minor dislocation and curvature.
And the hip joint is displaced in four ways: when it is displaced inward, or outward, or forward, or backward.
And it is most often displaced in the joints inside, and less frequently in the front or rear joints.
The sign of dislocation in the inner joints is this: when you straighten the patient's leg towards the healthy side, the diseased side becomes longer and more prominent than the healthy one, and the patient cannot bend their foot towards the anus due to the pain. This is where the post-dislocated anus becomes cauterized from the heat, so that the head of the bone has already been affected here.
The sign of the condition in which dislocation occurs, whether inside or outside, is that the conditions of the disease are contrary to this accident.
The sign of dislocation occurring in the front joints is that the patient extends their leg completely, but still feels pain on the affected side, and if they attempt to walk, it becomes difficult. Their urine is retained, and the anus becomes cauterized; they must lie on their side for healing.
And the sign of a dislocation in the rear parts is that it does not extend the pain, nor can it bend opposite to the bent knee, and the leg's position is shorter than the other, and the joint becomes soft, and the end of the limb points to that place.
The main reduction for this dislocation is that you consider, if the dislocation is old and ancient, it has already been reduced by itself or properly treated with rest and according to its position, then it is not in need of further treatment; thus, there is no need for any additional provision.
For those in which the dislocation is recent and it belongs to one of the four types of dislocations, you must do as follows: return the joint to its place and extend it both inward and outward, and turn it to the right and left, so that it strongly returns and does not need other treatment.
Perhaps, if it does not return in this manner, you will need to prepare a strong assistant and extend the bed of the patient beyond them, or apply more bindings, or a linen which is tight over the pain, and another assistant extends their hand from that side so as to place their hands behind the patient's thighs; and another tightly binds the limb at its joint, and another minister holds the end of the binding.
And if it is an extension of the patient or of the limb within the angle of the fork, or behind the back at the base of the spine.
And it is the extension of all these at once, so long as the patient's pain is elevated to their chest and hangs pendulously.
And this type of extension is specially important for all four (extremities).
And so if the dislocation returns to what we have said, it will be good; otherwise, it will be necessary for every kind of case to speak of its own treatment.
In the reduction of the hernia, when it is dislocated and the dislocation occurs within the folds, the patient should be placed on their side; then, the ligaments should be tightened around the base of the fold in the area between the top of the hernia and the point where the pain begins; and finally, the ligament should be extended from the painful area to the highest part of the fork.
Then, another assistant should firmly grasp the patient's thighs and press the swollen area of the affected thigh, extending outwards with great force, so that it returns to its place.
And this type of treatment is for the more delicate cure, whereby this member is returned to its place, unlike other types of treatment.
If the patient cannot stand on their feet due to this type of treatment, then both feet of the patient must be tied together with a strong ligature, lighter than usual, on both legs and both toes.
And the length of each part should be such that it is four times the width of the other, and the affected leg should be extended more than the other by a factor of two.
Then the hernia should be suspended over the top of the leg, and placed in the lower part; and the length of it should be from the ground two arms' lengths.
Then command a strong young person to reduce the head of the hernia, and hang the other hernia from another young person, while the other young person gently pushes the hernia back into place with firm pressure, so that the joint returns to its location quickly.
In the proper reduction, when there is a dislocation from its normal position, it is necessary to keep the patient immobile on their side as we have recommended in the case of a dislocated joint; and tighten the ligament specifically around the injured thigh and on their chest.
Then use two sticks as supports: one on the patient's feet and another on their head; and place a moist cloth around the middle of the thigh where the hernia is located to prevent damage while keeping the extension of the parts below from being pulled.
And each assistant should extend their part, and the doctor with his hand guides the reduction according to art (or skill).
And when the dislocation is in the front parts, you should ensure that the leg is extended slightly, and according to this method, the doctor places the palm of his right hand on the affected joint, then he tightens with his other hand, and by applying this pressure, he reduces the dislocation.
And if the dislocation is in the back parts, you should not extend the patient on the side, but elevate him above the ground; once you have established that he is resting on a hard surface, thus as we said about the position of the body when one joint is dislocated to the outside, and according to what we said about stretching the ligaments, there should be no harm.
And it should be administered compression with a splint on the area where the joint is dislocated.
Therefore, when the reduction is complete according to need â€” and the sign of the reduction of the hernia is not hidden from you, since you extend two thighs from the patient and when you see those folds and the hernia extrudes its thigh and you expand your excuse, then you know that the member according to need has returned â€” and now you arrange two things and place a bandage and pull out a bandage so that the opening is not worsened in any of the parts; and keep the patient at rest for three days or four.
Then carefully remove the ligature and the bandage, and compare one thigh to the other.
Now, if you see those folds in appearance, then you will know that the dislocation is already healed, and therefore release the patient.
And if you see any sign of softening, then return and bandage that, pull out that according to your initial stretch, and release it in three days.
And then gently pull it, causing the patient to walk slowly on some surface for a few days, until it is healed.
**Chapter XXXII**
**On the Treatment of Dislocated Joints**
A dislocated joint can occur in three ways: when it is pushed out of place, when it is pulled inward, and when it moves to the side, but it is not dislocated when it is pushed forward.
And the sign of a dislocated joint is that you command the patient to apply pressure on the affected area; then you know that the joint is dislocated.
And the restoration of dislocated joints is to cease the patient's pressure immediately, so that he extends his limb as much as possible; to hold his thigh against his chest, and to rest his foot between his legs; and then to press the dislocated joint firmly in your palm, and to interlock your fingers over the joint on both sides of the dislocation, and to stretch out your arm until the joint returns to its place.
And the sign of recovery is that their leg adheres to the thigh in a non-painful position.
Then apply a plaster to adhere the leg to the thigh, and then bind those parts with a bandage for three or four days, and then remove the bandage.
And do not use the patient's mobility for some days, until they are healed and comfortable.
If the reduction of the hernia is not urgent, then administer plenty of extensions to the laments of which treatment of the mentioned hernia has been previously described.
Chapter .XXXIII.
On the treatment of the dislocation of the talus.
Sometimes the ankle is remedied by a slight removal, and sometimes it is dislocated completely; the dislocation occurs either within the joints or outside them.
And the sign of the dislocation is that the ankle swells proceeding to the part where it is dislocated.
The treatment for the dislocation is with gentle reduction, and it should be extended to facilitate movement of the muscles and bones, and then wrapped until it heals.
But in the cure when it is completely dislocated, it is necessary to cease the pain immediately, and have a strong and able minister at the back of the body at the middle part of the dislocation.
And then you should place your right hand on the top of the foot from the dominant side, and your left hand below the foot at the location of the ankle.
And then gently pull the foot towards you with your right hand, and with your left make two movements, then extend your left hand; push the foot of the patient towards the bed on the opposite side from the leg that is working.
And do this two times as we have counted.
And on the third movement, push the foot of the patient towards the bed, and you are at the ankle.
So if you return in one movement or two according to this manner, and turn the foot inside out, it is good; otherwise, continue the operation over that part.
If you are forbidden from reducing it in this manner that we have recommended, then have the patient lie on their back on the ground, and stretch out a hard piece of wood over their chest, and press between their thighs, and wrap them tightly with a cloth so that the hernia does not escape.
And then the practitioner should hold the patient's legs, and another minister should extend the foot along its toes or with the aid of a ligature placed on the collar of the foot; and he should stretch out each minister in opposition to the extension of his part, and the padding between the thighs of the patient should retain him, so that the matter of the hernia is not drawn into the folds left beyond its extension.
Then the physician should re-align the dislocation with his hands, and another minister should hold the healthy thigh away from the affected side, so that the dislocation returns to its natural position.
And when the dislocation returns to its place and it is determined that the reduction is successful, then apply a plaster and reinforce those ligaments strongly, and tie the foot with ligament to the leg.
And be careful of the nerves that are behind the sole of the foot, so that the ligament over it is not violent and damages those parts strongly.
And then place a poultice on it for two days or three; if the inflammation subsides, remove the poultice.
And on the third day or the fourth, remove the poultice; and forbid the patient from moving for forty days. If it becomes necessary to move the patient from that position, there is a risk that the dislocation will not heal properly and become corrupted, and this can prevent recovery.
And if an abscess forms, then apply what we have mentioned about treatment and immersion in the place where it occurred, rather than other remedies, as long as it is healed.
Chapter .xxxiiii.
On the treatment of dislocation of the joints of the feet.
Know that one who is dislocated should be splinted to a certain extent for their treatment; and what is not difficult, it is quickly healed.
If the dislocation is in some sensitive part of the foot, then you should make the patient lie down with their foot elevated either on a pillow or table, and keep it that way as if they were walking.
And then you stand by the foot, place your hand over what threatens the joints, and gently press the foot towards the affected area until it returns to its normal position, and you observe that it is splinted and does not appear in the prominent location.
And then you place a board under the patient's foot that takes all the weight, which has two ends, and gently tighten the structure decently and firmly for three days; and afterwards, you remove it and make them rest from walking for several days, until they are completely healed and free from pain.
Chapter .xxxv.
Of the types of dislocation that are caused by illness or fracture or any other injury.
When any of these causes occurs and you perceive yourself in the task of healing it and restoring it, you often end up succumbing to death.
And for this reason, one should not presumptuously assume that anyone capable of healing is knowledgeable in the art, but rather those who have long studied it, with mercy and compassion; late, not hasty, and who use cautery only when necessary, leaving the judgment to divine will, unless one hopes for salvation from perdition and relief from suffering, and in whom there appears some hope. And therefore one should strive as much as possible to reduce it at the beginning of the cause, before applying cautery.
And when the member returns to its normal state, administer treatment with gentle care and cure the pain with moist poultices as appropriate for it.
If a dislocation is accompanied by a fracture and occurs in the joints where bones are separated, then you must drill through their statements and do as we have said for simple ailments of this kind that precede in the places of those.
And beware and avoid, according to your virtue, the instrument in the ways of fear as it is preceded by my prediction; for it is better for you to honor your Creator, maintain your glory, and heal your true body with those things at the right time. Thus, ends the words of Albucasim perfectly, from which God be blessed. Amen.
